    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a017c8a9-6601-4234-a16c-3e9da0af0a9a'

  <span id="freeText18199285404881049550" style="display:none">Neil Josten is the newest addition to the Palmetto State University Exy team. He's short, he's fast, he's got a ton of potential—and he's the runaway son of the murderous crime lord known as The Butcher.<br /><br />Signing a contract with the PSU Foxes is the last thing a guy like Neil should do. The team is high profile and he doesn't need sports crews broadcasting pictures of his face around the nation. His lies will hold up only so long under this kind of scrutiny and the truth will get him killed.<br /><br />But Neil's not the only one with secrets on the team. One of Neil's new teammates is a friend from his old life, and Neil can't walk away from him a second time. Neil has survived the last eight years by running. Maybe he's finally found someone and something worth fighting for.</span>

        rated it

  <span id="freeText10107050390665321739" style="display:none"><b>the book of no.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408111084ra/10808181.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>no, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[teenagers are not typically ushered into nightclubs to knock back shots. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, the NCAA would never permit <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[antipsychotics don't actually get you high like that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, you don't go from <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[come-down to withdrawal to i-will-fucking-kill-you within four hours of your last crazy-pill. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, marginally post-pubescent children wouldn't be able to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[set their mom's dead body on fire with gasoline and then bury the bones on the beach without getting caught once during the entire multi-hour operation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>—and who <i>does</i> that, anyway?<br><br>no, the human body cannot be reduced to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[charred bones <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[belongs to your crazy mom. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, you probably can't <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[drive a car for hundreds of miles while suffering the effects of a ruptured <i>anything</i>, never mind <i>everything,</i> not even if your kid is in the car with a book of matches and a gas can. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, there is no team sport on earth that can be competently played if <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[its team members are as likely to get into a fistfight with one another as with the opposing team <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>—baseball and the 1979 yankees notwithstanding. <br><br>no, you can't shake off the effects of a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[concussion and climb out the window the next day after a minor coma spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the yakuza do not have and never fucking came close to having a toehold in the carolinas. or new york. or san possible to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>play a fucking contact sport with knives strapped to your body</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>—and who seriously fucking does <i>that,</i> ever, anywhere, anyway?<br><br>no, you can't really <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[make up your own sport <i>and</i> your own recreational drugs in the same novel without sounding like you know nothing that is actually true about either sports <i>or</i> drugs. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, you probably can't make this big melodramatic speech with your <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[melodramatic fingers distending your melodramatic mouth—the entire melodramatic time you're speaking melodramatically. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>no, <i>one does not simply walk into mordor.</i><br><br>no.<br><br>okay?<br><br>just—no.<br><br><br><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

<div id="review_1521058605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521058605" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1521058605?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1521058605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8471488150985883593"><b>read 3 [janaury 2020]</b><br/>starting off my year right with these idiots 😌rereads are the best for appreciating details you didn't catch the first times, and the biggest things I came away from with this reread were: (a) Neil genuinely forgetting people could be normal height after spending so long around Andrew, and (b) that oNE TIME Andrew protects Neil before they've even struck the deal 🥺what are these emotions, unasked for, i cannot.<br/><br/><b>read 2 [february 2019]</b><br/>I am just here to raise both hands in the a</span>
  <span id="freeText8471488150985883593" style="display:none"><b>read 3 [janaury 2020]</b><br />starting off my year right with these idiots 😌rereads are the best for appreciating details you didn't catch the first times, and the biggest things I came away from with this reread were: (a) Neil genuinely forgetting people could be normal height after spending so long around Andrew, and (b) that oNE TIME Andrew protects Neil before they've even struck the deal 🥺what are these emotions, unasked for, i cannot.<br /><br /><b>read 2 [february 2019]</b><br />I am just here to raise both hands in the air and admit<b> I am hella obsessed with this series.</b> I've been craving a reread since I finished in feb last year...and omgsosghso being back with my Fox sons is just everything. I love these characters. I love the complexity, subplots, subtext and utter attitude problems of these disaster kids with their who have more scarring and ptsd than their tiny statures can handle. (And yes, they are tiny. Shout out to Andrew who is 5ft and literally shorter than me by one inch. FINALLY I'M TALLER THAN SOMEONE.) <br /><br />and i'm obsessed. i'm dying. leave me to analyse every single thing that comes out of Andrew's mouth in this book because O H B O Y does it hit in a different light now that you know his Feelings™ for a certain someone.<br /><br />also Neil is absolutely an argumentative little shit and I love him to death<br /><br />(also the audiobook is so good!! and the audiobook's cover is amazing!! why can't we have that cover everywhere!!)<br /><br /><br />*:·ﾟ✧*:·ﾟ✧<br /><b>Read 1 || February 2018</b><br /><br /><br /><b>Holy wow that was super intense.</b> I've had this on my TBR for absolutely forever and I swear, I started reading it and 2 minutes later I knew (a) I wouldn't be able to stop, and (b) I was going to need to read the rest ah hahahah. (YES I JUST BOUGHT THE SEQUEL TWO SECONDS AGO.)<br /><br />Moving forward.<br /><br /><b>THINGS TO EXPECT FROM THIS BOOK:</b><br />• a bucket load of absolutely horrible characters<br />• literally everyone should be in therapy but ok<br />• somehow they're awful but it's like??? I can't look away???<br />• Neil is an absolute precious cinnamon son<br />• there is a hybrid sport called Exy (kind of like lacrosse)<br />• there's a lot of college flotsam happening<br />• THERE'S AN UNDERCURRENT OF GANG WARS AND DARKNESS<br />• blood<br />• bad decisions<br />• unhealthy relationships<br />• absolutely gripping writing<br />• nasty boys protecting each other like nothing else because family don't end in blood, son *<br /><br /><br />* um yeah I just quoted supernatural I don't even know anymore<br /><br /><b>I see a lot of people comparing this to The Raven Cycle and like? I <i>sort</i> of get it. But also no.</b> Just because it's about a bunch of broken boys doesn't really make it Ravenish!! But I also LIKE reading about bunches of broken boys so there's that.<br /><br /><b>Although there's hella problematic things going on in here.</b><br />I mean these teens do treat each other like trash a lot. Andrew is basically a sociopath (probably?!) and horrific. And I was NOT happy with a lot of the problematic elements. Like the overuse of the word r*tard (can you not...ever again) then in the nightclub <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Andrew drugs Neil against his will and Nicky kisses him against his will, which is absolutely sexual assault. Like maybe Neil didn't hate it, but he didn't give permission for it. <u>Therefore it is not okay.</u>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <b>But while there were problematic things in the book, I don't think it ever was condoning them.</b> And that's the difference right? Like this book is full of hella broken boys and awful things happening and Neil does NOT brush off their nonsense.<br /><br />(Also I'm not sure why this book is being shelved as lgbt, unless Things™ happen later on?? So far there's no romance for Neil. Not <i>so</i> sure who I'd ship him with yet but I have Thoughts™.)<br /><br /><b>CAN WE TALK ABOUT NEIL.</b><br />He's scarred and damaged and on the run and fajdkslafd (coincidentally reminds me of a character I've written so I'm completely adoring of him) and just the way he reacts when someone offers to take care of him and he's like ???? Mind blown. He is PRECIOUS. And I wish him to stay alive that'd be nice.<br /><br />Also shout out to the coach for being the mother of these 10 delinquent idiots of the Fox team. Because they're literally like:<br /><blockquote>Coach: I hate you all.<br />Coach: also here's some cereal and a blanket and did you get a good night's sleep? I will beat you with a spoon if you don't look after each other<br />Coach: now get out i hate you</blockquote><br /><br />#TEAMCOACHISAGOODMOTHER<br /><br /><b>The writing was also super addictive.</b><br />I'm not sure if it was a "this is a trainwreck and I can't look away" or what?! Like I don't <i>like</i> sporty books. I didn't even like Exy! BUT I LOVED THE BOOK TO DEATH STILL. Most of the sporty scenes were at least short (why is sport so aggressive holy heck) and if my attention blinked over them it didn't matter. <b>I was here for Neil's secrets and his complex relationship with Kevin and the way the relationships were all woven in messy knots.</b> It's so so character driven and that's what I like to read about.<br /><br /><b>So I mean, I just bought the sequel so guess what I'm doing this week.</b> GOODBYE I NEED TO GO SEE IF THESE PSYCHOTIC AND HORRIBLE CINNAMON SCONES KILL EACH OTHER OR NOT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8471488150985883593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2281728211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281728211" />
    <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments"><img alt="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554228831p2/67920559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281728211?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=mafia">mafia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=slow-burn">slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=family-power">family-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=thin-line-between-love-and-hate">thin-line-between-love-and-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=story-with-sports">story-with-sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=better-late-than-never">better-late-than-never</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281728211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6293578605501530076"><i>
  <b>"I can see it. You've got that look in your eye that says you know where every exit to this dormitory is."</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990569._SX540_.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><i>The Foxhole Court</i> was definitely a surprise, wherein I didn't get anything that I was expecting. However, I got a lot of which I didn't even know I needed. </b><br/><br/><u>Note</u>: All rights belong to the different artists that have created the (fucking amazing) fanart attached to this review.<br/>__________<br/><br/><u>
  <b>Meet The Foxes</b>
</u><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"The Palmetto State University Foxes were a team of talented rejects and junki</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6293578605501530076" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"I can see it. You've got that look in your eye that says you know where every exit to this dormitory is."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990569._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><i>The Foxhole Court</i> was definitely a surprise, wherein I didn't get anything that I was expecting. However, I got a lot of which I didn't even know I needed. </b><br><br><u>Note</u>: All rights belong to the different artists that have created the (fucking amazing) fanart attached to this review.<br>__________<br><br><u>
  <b>Meet The Foxes</b>
</u><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"The Palmetto State University Foxes were a team of talented rejects and junkies because Wymack only recruited athletes from broken homes. His decision to turn the Foxhole Court into a halfway house of sorts was nice in theory, but it meant his players were fractured isolationists who couldn't get along long enough to get through a game." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Danielle Leigh Wilds, #1 → Offensive Dealer <br>Kevin Day, #2 → Striker <br>Andrew Joseph Minyard, #3 → Goalkeeper <br>Matthew Donovan Boyd, #4 → Backliner <br>Aaron Michael Minyard, #5 → Backliner <br>Bryan Seth Gordon, #6 → Striker <br>Allison Jamaica Reynolds, #7 → Defensive Dealer <br>Nicholas Esteban Hemmick, #8 → Backliner <br>Natalie Renee Walker, #9 → Goalkeeper <br>Neil Josten, #10 → Striker</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Andrew bets you can outrun everyone on this team. Coach said you clocked a fourminute mile back in Arizona. That true? You're a little short to run so fast." <br>"I like running," Neil said. <br>"Fuck running," Seth said. "Learn to score. Word is you still can't score on Andrew." <br>"No," Neil admitted. "Not yet." <br>"When you do, you can talk to me," Seth said. "Until then, stay out of my way and try not to drag down my line too much." <br>"Welcome to the Foxhole Court," Matt added”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br> <br>For those of you who go into this and aren't familiar with Exy (the sport that the foxes, alongside a bunch of other teams play - it's broken down on the authors <a href="http://korakos.tumblr.com/fox" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a><br><br>I think the gang of misfits that all hated each other was one of the aspects of this book that I fucking loved. I can see how the comparisons with The Raven Cycle come in, especially with all the hardass and badass shenanigans that go around. <br>However, in a way it is way more deep than what is shown on the surface. We get elements that I wouldn't have even dreamt this book could cover. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"We have to talk. Something went wrong this morning." "We're Foxes. Something is always going wrong," Seth said, but he fished the remote out from</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>The LGBTQIA rep is phenomenal in its soft approach. We get the Mafia, mental health, crime and justice, family... and most importantly - teamwork with a team that is hellbent on not working.</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You lost. Your school is the laughingstock of the NCAA. You're a team with no concept of teamwork." <br>"Lucky for you," Neil said. "If we were a unified front you wouldn't have a chance against us." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Plot</b>
</u><br><br>The amount of hype that surrounds this series is something that you can't even put to words. With a fanbase that strong, one is cautious treading into the story. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990570._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So here I am, about to make an ass out of myself. <br>Although, I loved how character driven this plot was, I also felt like it was one of the story's shortcomings. It dragged on for quite a bit, and I only found myself getting into the story at about 75%. After reading a couple reviews on this however, I found that a lot of people say that the storyline reallllllyyyy picks up in the second and third book. Because I actually did like TFC quite a bit, I'm most probably going to read that this week if not next up. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>As much as the Foxes disliked each other at times, they disliked their opponents more. They were still too fractured to be truly great, but they were good enough to give him chills. Neil finally understood how the Foxes made it to third place last fall and scored a spot in championships.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The writing felt very mediocre, as it skipped through a lot of character names and it felt confusing following a heavy scene sometimes. I wish I could say it thrived through its amateur cliches, but...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990571._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Banter</b>
</u><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Coach says he's got potential." Matt looked at Neil. "Andrew says you're fast." <br>Neil frowned. "When did he say that?" <br>"When do you think, wiseass?" Seth asked. "We talked all kinds of shit about you after you booked it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The banter in this book was amazing to say the least. If I could rate the book only on the humor and the quirky hits we get between characters, it would hands down be a 5 star read. I also loved that the author integrated three girls on the team with completely opposing personalities to even out all the testosterone that was flying around. That goes without saying however, that each and every guy on the team had such a brutally honest and real persona to them, that the whole thing mixed together gave you the best fucking Exy team on the planet. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"We'll tell everyone you're there for conditional early practice. Chances are half of them will believe it. You won't be able to fool the rest, but that doesn't matter. Foxes are Foxes for a reason and they know we wouldn't sign you if you didn't qualify. That doesn't mean they know specifics. It's not my place to ask, and I'm sure as hell not going to tell them."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990572.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Furthermore, the dynamic between the coach and the kids was something I loved. I fucking loved Wymack, not just as a side character but as a coach! He was one of those characters that I was skeptical about in the beginning, but as I read chapters I slowly started to like him more and more. <br>Although, the dialogue was at times unrealistic, it was a very minor fallback in the grand scheme of things. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"All right," he said, then promptly forgot what he was saying when he got a good look at the back of the bus. "Damn it all to hell. Hemmick! You were supposed to wake them up ten miles ago." <br>"I don't want to die," Nicky said. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990573.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Neil and Andrew</b>
</u><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Hey, Pinocchio," he said without looking at Neil. The cheer in his voice was too mocking to be real, but Neil doubted anyone but the Foxes noticed. "Time to run. This one's for you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Someone scream 'slow burn' louder for the people at the back. <br><br>Andrew and Neil was something of a conundrum for me. During the first 3 quarters of the book, I really did not know how the writer was going to be able to pull the chemistry between the both of them off. It all seemed like a mess to me, and both of them did not look like they would be good together. <br><br>I really loved Andrew... he's still a mystery to me and I can't wait to slowly solve him through this trilogy. He is the foxes' "deadliest investment" and if that doesn't get you intrigued, then damn.... I thought I was a tough crowd. I also can't wait to read how Neil's time with the foxes unfolds, he is truly a cinnamon role that needs love and a family because fuck knows, he's suffered enough. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517591551i/24990574._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But then the last 25% of the book turned up, and it hit me like a bag of bricks. It's unconventionally perfect and I love how it was broken and not yet there and everything that a Young Adult book needs when there are so many serious overtones in it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“God damn it, Minyard. This is why we can't have nice things.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I also love when an author bends the rules of YA, and shows that it doesn't really take romance (or dense romance) for that matter, to make a book successful. The chemistry between the characters and the feeling of a group of misfits coming together to make something bigger <i>is enough</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Remember this feeling. This is the moment you stop being the rabbit."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Between the pep talks, powwows, bus rides and midnight practices - I could feel why so many people have fallen (like myself) in love with these group of outcasts just trying to live life. It's so much more than what you think it is and if you haven't already read it... then give these kids a chance. You (probably) won't regret it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You play like you have everything to lose."<br>"Welcome to the line."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6293578605501530076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1694047171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1694047171" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1694047171?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=sports">sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=college">college</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694047171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4631543348154842541">Who needs a TV drama when you have <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_' title='The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Foxhole Court</a>?<br/><br/>Danger, intensity, sports, addiction, illegal activity, reckless characters… <b>You have it all.</b><br/><br/>One thing you do not have, however, is this: romance. Not yet, anyway, though the author teases you here and there. The first time I picked it up, two years ago, I did so because I saw the theme ‘‘lgbt’’ in its book description, and I was desperately in need of a sexy gay ship.<br/><br/>And so when I read the first chapters and realized that no romance seemed to</span>
  <span id="freeText4631543348154842541" style="display:none">Who needs a TV drama when you have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a>?<br /><br />Danger, intensity, sports, addiction, illegal activity, reckless characters… <b>You have it all.</b><br /><br />One thing you do not have, however, is this: romance. Not yet, anyway, though the author teases you here and there. The first time I picked it up, two years ago, I did so because I saw the theme ‘‘lgbt’’ in its book description, and I was desperately in need of a sexy gay ship.<br /><br />And so when I read the first chapters and realized that no romance seemed to be developing between the main character and another guy, I started to lost interest.<br /><br />It takes time for it to appear, and even now I have no idea if it’s going where I think it is. <br /><br />But seeing how popular this series is, I decided to give a second chance, with my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/67405281-yusra" rel="nofollow noopener">Yusra</a>, this time without expecting anything.<br /><br />Boy was that the way to go. Going into a book having no expectations whatsoever means that there’s no way you can be crushed with disappointment. First time I tried reading it two years ago, I gave it a one-star-rating, so it could only go up from there. <br /><br />This story is crazy, as are the majority of the characters. And they all have such a huge presence in the story that it’s hard to not notice them or pay them no mind.<br /><br />They are messed up in their own respective ways. No one is perfect. That’s the point… bringing together a group of misfits that both hate and love each other and train them to become one single family on the field.<br /><br />Well that needs additional work, but I’m excited to see them play some more. Funny thing is, I actually don’t bother with sports in real life, but somehow I was on the edge of my seat reading the sports-related scenes in this one. <br /><br />Now I really want to go on Amazon.ca and buy the hard copies and frame them and put them on my bedroom walls and stare at them every night before going to sleep... and what is happening to me?<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4631543348154842541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2600604566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11985587785182404839"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548197864i/26957155._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It's about second chances, Neil. Second, third, fourth, whatever, as long as you get at least one more than what anyone else wanted to give you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>First and foremost, I want to thank <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68157476-may' rel='nofollow noopener'>May</a> for giving me the emotional support I needed while reading this book:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548378627i/26966966.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Secondly, holy shit, I didn’t think I’d actually like this. What even is my life? Friends, I couldn’t put this down. I read it in 24 hours and no regrets were had. This was way darker than I expected, but I became so damn invested in</span>
  <span id="freeText11985587785182404839" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548197864i/26957155._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It's about second chances, Neil. Second, third, fourth, whatever, as long as you get at least one more than what anyone else wanted to give you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>First and foremost, I want to thank <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68157476-may" rel="nofollow noopener">May</a> for giving me the emotional support I needed while reading this book:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548378627i/26966966.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Secondly, holy shit, I didn’t think I’d actually like this. What even is my life? Friends, I couldn’t put this down. I read it in 24 hours and no regrets were had. This was way darker than I expected, but I became so damn invested in this main character and I honestly fell in love with him and his story from day one. I know this is a bit of a polarizing read, but if you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2415998038" rel="nofollow noopener">Fence</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2453722508" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicker King</a> then I think this story is for sure worth a try for you! Especially since it’s <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00E9BLRUI/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=meltotheany-20&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;creativeASIN=B00E9BLRUI&amp;linkId=d723f5510abbc7f043522affd5e08ded" rel="nofollow noopener">free on Amazon US</a>! <br><br>Basically, this is a story about a boy that has been on the run practically his entire life. Neil is currently living in a small town in Arizona, trying to stay on the down low, but he can’t stay away from his one love; Exy, which is a sport that is sort of a mix of Lacrosse and Soccer. But Neil is homeless, able to fit all his possessions in a duffel bag and is currently sneaking into his school’s gym to sleep. But his Exy coach notices where he has been sleeping, but he also notices the pure talent that Neil harnesses on the Exy field and sends a video to possible college recruiters. <br><br>And the Foxes from Palmetto State University’s Exy team like what they see when they come and recruit Neil. PSU is a newly reformed and up-and-coming team, who are known for taking in kids who normally don’t get second chances, but they are even more hyped this upcoming season because they now have Kevin Day (AKA: The Son of Exy) playing for them. Neil knows the smartest move is to stay out of the spotlight, but he is so very tired of running, especially running from the only thing that brings him happiness.<br><br>But friends, I fell in love with these players so damn quickly: <br><br>➽ <b>Neil Josten</b> - Ready to fight for and protect at all costs.<br>➽ <b>Andrew Minyard</b> - Still sus and I’m still not sold on. <br>➽ <b>Aaron Minyard</b> - No opinion yet, but I know all my friends hate.<br>➽ <b>Allison Reynolds</b> - Badass princess that I stan. <br>➽ <b>Nicky Hemmick</b> - The actual best. <br>➽ <b>Seth Gordon</b> - My fucking face when. <br>➽ <b>Renee Walker</b> - My chill pacifist who I already adore completely. <br>➽ <b>Matt Boyd</b> - My heartwarming pure boy. <br>➽ <b>Dan Wilds</b> - My actual queen.<br>➽ <b>Kevin Day</b> - My actual king. My favorite Fox. Also, the thing I am most invested with in this entire story is him and Riko and everything that went down and everything that is going to go down. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548378627i/26966967.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548378627i/26966968._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Breathtaking art by <a href="http://llstarcasterll.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">llstarcasterll</a>!) <br><br>But besides these foxes, who I mostly adore, my favorite part of this book was just seeing Neil tired of feeling like he didn’t have a home, and finally not only accepting that fact, but willing to finally carve out something for himself, completely and utterly unapologetically. Again, I’m not saying that what Neil is doing is the healthiest of circumstances, but seeing him realize that he is worthy of a home, of a family, and of love, was just so damn beautiful. And I know that this is just going to increase during the next two books! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Hope was a dangerous, disquieting thing, but he thought perhaps he liked it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, I just really couldn’t put this down. This is for sure a very character driven book. And I’ll be the first to say that these characters are for sure mostly morally grey and they do a lot of sus shit. But… my love for Kevin and Neil just overpowered all the other questionable teammates. But I’ll talk to you all later, because I am immediately picking up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2687740322" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>! <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for a lot of drug use, talk of overdosing, underage drinking, loss of a loved one, talk of suicide, mention of cutting, drugging someone, jokes about rape, physical abuse, talk of past parental abuse, ableist insults, homophobic slurs (the f word), and use of the r word.<br><br>🦊 Also, this <a href="https://jamishelves.wordpress.com/2018/08/03/film-adaptation-friday-the-foxhole-court-by-nora-sakavic/" rel="nofollow noopener">film adaption fan-cast by Jamieson</a> added ten years to my life. <br><br>Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/69919640-sol-thebookishking" rel="nofollow noopener">Sol</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13507409-amy" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a>! 🧡</span>
  <a data-text-id="11985587785182404839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2058937174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2058937174" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2058937174?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2058937174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8923423298361307269"><i>”Easy, easy.” Andrew lifted his hands in a careless shrug. “Why bother? It’s a cruel world, right Neil? You wouldn’t be here if it wasn’t.”<br/>“It’s not the world that’s cruel,” Neil said. “It’s the people in it.”</i><br/><br/>trigger warnings: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[drug abuse, a character being drugged against his will, physical child abuse, violence, emotional abuse, bullying, dysfunctional relationships, sexual assault <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>I don’t know why I waited three freaking years to read this, but I could really kick</span>
  <span id="freeText8923423298361307269" style="display:none"><i>”Easy, easy.” Andrew lifted his hands in a careless shrug. “Why bother? It’s a cruel world, right Neil? You wouldn’t be here if it wasn’t.”<br />“It’s not the world that’s cruel,” Neil said. “It’s the people in it.”</i><br /><br />trigger warnings: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[drug abuse, a character being drugged against his will, physical child abuse, violence, emotional abuse, bullying, dysfunctional relationships, sexual assault <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don’t know why I waited three freaking years to read this, but I could really kick myself for procrastinating so long! Then again maybe it’s good I waited so long because I’m pretty sure my younger self would have gobbled this book down like nobody’s business and then would have regretted not giving it the attention it deserves! *lol* <br /><br />So yes, I’m three years wiser now and even though I learned to savour books I still had a really tough time trying not to rush through this, because people! THIS IS SO GOOD!!!! Yes, I know, I know! It’s no Shakespear or Wilde, but even though there isn’t a lot of plot or background to go with this fictional world there is something it definitely has going for itself! Its amazing characters and Exy!!! And boy did I love both! XD It’s been a long time I got so consumed by a book and I think it’s mostly due to the super intriguing characters. <br /><br /><b>“The Foxhole Court”</b> is nothing but character driven and ahh do I love books like that! *lol* I mean if you’re looking for logic or sophisticated words this most definitely isn’t the right book for you, but if you decide to leave your logic at the front door and dive into this without overthinking it too much instead: Well, then you’re in for a real treat! I guess to some degree you should actually read this book like it’s a game. Enjoy the rush of the moment, follow your instincts, trust your heart and thoroughly ignore the voice at the back of your mind. ;-P If you follow those instructions you might be able to enjoy it as much as I did. *lol* <br /><br />And since I can’t wait to gush about all those lovely characters I’ll call it a day now and just jump into my character’s section instead! XD<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>You are now a student at Palmetto State University, so tread carefully and don’t enter the Foxes dorms. If you don’t head this well-intentioned advice you’ll be confronted with a bunch of spoilers that might ruin the fun for you! Coach Wymack says: Don’t say I didn’t warn you! ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Neil Josten:</b><br /><br /><i>”This was the only thing he had left that was real. Now that he’d had a taste of it again, he didn’t know how to walk away from it.”</i> <br /><br />I swear Neil Josten is a precious baby bean and everyone who wants to hurt him will have to go through me first! &lt;333 I mean it! This boy is so sweet and innocent and this even though so many horrible things happened to him. He needs to be protected at all costs and I’m ready to defend him with my life! I love Neil so, so much and I hated that he was so down and broken at the beginning of the book. I mean that boy didn’t even have any hope and then the Foxes found him and BAM his life took a 180 degree spin and never stopped moving ever since. Also his character development was amazing! At first he’s so very careful and guarded, he’s so afraid of taking a wrong step that he doesn’t even allow himself to breath. Well, and then he joins the Foxes and his true character gets a chance to come out. And boy, did I love the boy he hid inside!! Neil can be so sassy and vigorous! I had no idea! &lt;3 I want more of this Neil and to be entirely honest I can’t wait to pick up the next book! ;-) My kicked puppy is turning into a true <s>lion</s> fox and I need that new Neil like I need air to breath! XD<br /><br /><i>”Keys meant Neil had explicit permission to be here and do what he liked. They meant he belonged.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Neil stepped over it and went to stand in front of Wymack: within arm’s reach but just barely. He’d perfected that trick as a kid. He could look at anyone’s arms and judge the safe distance from them in a heartbeat. If they had to move to hit him, he had enough time to dodge. Either way he wouldn’t catch the full intended force of their blow.”</i><br /><br /><i>Riko’s smile could have frozen hell. “I am not scared of Kevin. I know him.”<br />“You’re going to eat those words,” Neil said. “You’re going to choke on them.”</i><br /><br /><b>Andrew Minyard:</b><br /><br /><i>”Oh,” Andrew said. “Oh, you might actually turn out to be interesting. For a little while, at least. I don’t think the amusement will last. It never does.”</i><br /><br />I know about half of the people who will read this will be like WTH?! But I’ll still say it anyway: <b>I LOVE AND ADORE ANDREW MINYARD THAT LITTLE SHIT!!!</b> *lol* Yes, his character is problematic and shady af but I don’t care! XD That controlling, bitchy and crazy bastard won over my heart the moment he appeared on page and even though I hated that he drugged Neil I still kind of get why he did it?! Most people will say he’s a psycho and even though that might be true, he’s still a psycho with a big heart. Andrew loves his family and he would do anything for them! Yes, he’d even go to the length of drugging a person he sees as a threat just to make sure that she/he isn’t. Andrew is fiercely protective of the people he loves and cares about and I can relate to that. So you might say I understand the person that’s hidden behind all those carefully crafted layers of craziness. His character is very intriguing and I’m sure there is so much more to him than initially meets the eye. Is it totally illogical and unrealistic that a person that’s so small (5ft, we’re talking 5ft here, people) is as intimidating and dangerous as Andrew? Yes, but it’s fun nevertheless and we all know that even the smallest person can pack a punch. ;-P I want more of him. Period!!! &lt;3<br /><br /><i>”Let Andrew give you things if he wants to. He’s not normally the gifting type, so it’s kind of fun.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”Oh, he made it,” Andrew said. “That’s interesting.”<br />He pressed two fingers to Neil’s throat, checking his pulse. When Neil tried to bat him away, Andrew caught his wrist with his free hand. His smile was small and fierce as he leaned forward into Neil’s space. <br />“Remember this feeling. This is the moment you stop being the rabbit.”</i><br /><br /><b>Coach Wymack:</b><br /><br /><i>”Did you think I made the team the way it is because I thought it would be a good publicity stunt? It’s about second chances, Neil. Second, third, fourth, whatever, as long as you get at least one more than what anyone else wanted to give you.”</i> <br /><br />I really liked Coach Wymack because even though his players don’t seem to see it, it’s obvious that he has a big heart! This man cares for his team and he’s providing them with a safe environment to spread their wings. Something tells me that someone gave him a second, third or even fourth chance when he was younger and that he’s trying to do the same for the members of his team. I hope we’ll find out more about his past in the other books and I’m definitely ready to dive into his background story. =) Coach Wymack is the best! <br /><br /><b>Kevin Day:</b><br /><br /><i>”Tetsuji took Kevin in and took over his training, but he also gave Kevin to Riko – literally. Kevin isn’t human to them. He’s a project. He’s a pet, and it’s Riko’s name on his leash. The fact he ran away is a miracle. If Tetsuji called tomorrow and told him to come home, Keven would. He knows what Tetsuji would do to him if he refused. He’d be too afraid to say no.”</i><br /><br />I’m going to be honest here: Kevin is still an enigma to me and even though he’s an integral part of the story because of his connection to Neil I still didn’t get a feel for his character. If you ask me that’s mostly due to the fact that he rarely talks and that he lives in his own world. Exy is everything for him and everything else that’s around him isn’t important if it doesn’t have to do with the sport. *lol* So yep, all I know is that Exy is Kevin’s life and that he was raised as Riko’s peronal toy. Maybe that’s even the reason why his character is so bland. He never got a chance to do what HE wanted to do and therefore never was able to develop his own character. Guess I’ll have to continue with the series to see some of his true self. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”If you won’t play with me, you’ll play for me,” Kevin said. “You’re never going to get there on your own, so give your game to me.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Riko Moriyama:</b><br /><br /><i>Riko jerked back a bit in surprise, started to school his expression into something more civil, and gave up when he realized who had joined them.<br />“We were just talking about you,” Riko said.<br />“With your fists, it seems,” Andrew said. “Don’t touch my things, Riko. I don’t share.”</i><br /><br />Now here’s a character I instantly disliked! XD Riko is so smug and full of himself that I just wanted to punch him in his face! Thankfully Neil already did that for me. Verbally but still! *lol* I can’t believe Kevin was raised with Riko and I feel very sorry for him. To be in the shadow of such a guy must have hurt and the fact that he broke his hand... *shakes head* Some part of me really hopes that Riko will be put in his place and I’m about a 100% sure we’ll say way more of him in those other books than we actually want to. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Neil &amp; Andrew:</u><br /><br /><i>”Your loose ends aren’t adding up.”<br />“I’m not a math problem.”<br />“But I’ll still solve you.”</i><br /><br /><b>THOSE TWO!!!! I SHIP THEM SO HARD AND I SHIP THEM LIKE THERE’LL BE NO TOMORROW!!</b> *lol* I mean honestly!! Their chemistry! The way they interact, all those little subtle nuances in their conversations, those seemingly insignificant and infinitesimal touches. I saw it between Ronan and Adam and I’m seeing it here!!! This ship is going to sail and BURNNN BRIGHT!!! And I’m so here to see it! &lt;333 Also I kind of love how Andrew always seems to be pulled towards Neil when he’s in his orbit!! Did anyone realize how often he’s leaning closer to him because I certainly did!!! I want those two to give into their feelings ... badly... very badly! *lol* And I hope that Andrew will let Neil in as much as Neil let him in. I mean at the end of the book he basically entrusted him with his life and I want ... no actually I NEED Andrew to open up to Neil! Gosh I just need more of them and I’m beginning to realize that I’m total Neil &amp; Andrew trash! *LOL* <br /><br /><i>Neil tensed as Andrew’s fingers wrapped around the back of his neck, but Andrew only wanted to pull Neil’s head down. Neil focused on Andrew’s cheekbone so as not to go cross-eyed and let Andrew study his eyes.<br />“Another bit of unexpected honesty,” Andrew said. “Any particular reason?”<br />“Nicky asked nicely. You might try it sometime.”<br />“We already talked about this. I don’t ask.” Andrew gave Neil another slow once-over and let go.</i><br /><br /><i>”What would it take to make you stay?”<br />The question was so unexpected Neil had to turn back. “What?”<br />Andrew laughed quietly at his shock and leaned forward. “Name it and it’s yours. It doesn’t matter what it is so long as you stand your ground here with us.”<br />“I can’t.”<br />“You can. You have everything you need to survive. You’re just too afraid to see it.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He knows what it’s like to hate every day of his life, to wake up afraid every day, but he’s got you at his back telling him everything’s going to be okay. He has everything, even when he’s lost everything, and I’m – “ Neil didn’t want to say it, but the word was already there, broken and pathetic between them, “nothing. I’ll always have and be nothing.”<br />Andrew reached up and forcibly uncurled Neil’s fingers from his mouth. He pushed Neil’s hand out of the way and stared Neil down with nothing between them. Neil didn’t understand the look on his face. There was no censure over Neil’s crooked parents or pity for their deaths, no triumph over having backed Neil into admitting so much, and no obvious skepticism for such an outlandish story. Whatever this look was, it was dark and intense enough to swallow Neil whole.</i><br /><br /><i>”A group of people shouldered their way up to the bar counter at Neil’s back, pushing him into Andrew. Andrew didn’t budge beneath his weight. He was something solid to lean against, something violent and fierce and unmoving. Neil couldn’t remember what it felt like to have someone hold him up. It was terrifying and liberating all at once. His life was out of his control now; he was giving it to Andrew and hoping Andrew would keep it safe.”</i><br /><br /><u>Kevin &amp; Andrew:</u><br /><br /><i>”Help me,” Kevin said, almost a whisper.<br />Andrew clucked his tongue and cocked his head to one side. “Help you? Help a man who lies to my face for a month? How?”<br />“I want to stay,” Kevin said. “I’ll ask you again: don’t let him take me away.”<br />“You’re the one who would tell him yes,” Andrew said. “Maybe you forgot.”</i><br /><br />Those two have such an intriguing dynamic! I really don’t know what’s going on between them and why Kevin trusts Andrew so much but I’m more than just ready to solve that mystery! Also I hope one day it will be explained why everyone has so much respect of Andrew. Even Riko has respect and considering he’s the baddie of the story this is interesting! What did Andrew do??!! And what exactly is his deal with Kevin?! Because they definitely made some sort of deal, I just have no idea what it might entail. I need answers. XD<br /><br /><u>Neil &amp; Riko:</u><br /><br /><i>”I will ask you only once to tone down that animosity.”<br />“I can’t,” Neil said. “I have a bit of an attitude problem.”<br />Riko’s smile was all ice. “A bit?”</i><br /><br />And here comes my favourite part of the entire book! I LOVED how Neil put Riko into his place during the TV interview!!! GOSH! That scene was EVERYTHING and if that’s Neil’s true self I’m really desperate to see more of him! &lt;3 I swear Neil giving Riko a run for his money is my new aesthetic! *lol* I, for my part, wouldn’t mind to read more about Neil’s “attitude problem”, yet at the same time I’m kind of afraid what Riko will do. He won’t accept this and some part of me is worried that he’ll hurt my precious baby bean. &gt;_&lt; Ahh! I really need to read book two! <br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I never expected to love this so much but right from the very first sentence this world drew me in, locked the door and threw the key away. In short: I’ve been a goner the moment I started to read this and I’m afraid my addiction will only get even worse. XD Yes, this sometimes reads like fan fiction and yes, the mental health rep in this is more than just a little sketchy (if not completely unrealistic, weird and – I’m no expert - wrong) but as I already pointed out earlier in my review: This is not a book to read with your mind, this is a book you’ll have to read following your gut instinct. So all told this book is problematic af, kind of unrealistic and definitely politically incorrect in so many different ways and on so many levels... but I still loved it!? O_o On to the next one! *lol*</span>
  <a data-text-id="8923423298361307269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2255792511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2255792511" />
    <a title="♡ the belle and the book ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book"><img alt="♡ the belle and the book ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605284490p2/22594701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2255792511?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♡ the belle and the book ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♡ the belle and the book ♡" href="/user/show/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book">♡ the belle and the book ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18874651-the-foxhole-court">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=lgbtqiap-rep">lgbtqiap-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=lost-interest">lost-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=series-i-wont-continue">series-i-wont-continue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=cringe-worthy">cringe-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=highly-anticipated">highly-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=m-m-romance">m-m-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=ugh">ugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594701-the-belle-and-the-book?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255792511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9155843782683179058"><b>
  <blockquote>after what felt like 90 years after finishing this headache and slump-causing awful book, my tear-stained review is now up aaahhhhhh</blockquote>
</b><br/>First off, I just want to say that if you loved this book and you're my friend, there are no hard feelings for me. We all have different opinions and I hope you'll respect mine as I do yours. I still love you guys. Believe me when I say that I am deeply annoyed down to my soul that this book didn't work out for me. I was so ready to love this but shit happened. </span>
  <span id="freeText9155843782683179058" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>after what felt like 90 years after finishing this headache and slump-causing awful book, my tear-stained review is now up aaahhhhhh</blockquote>
</b><br>First off, I just want to say that if you loved this book and you're my friend, there are no hard feelings for me. We all have different opinions and I hope you'll respect mine as I do yours. I still love you guys. Believe me when I say that I am deeply annoyed down to my soul that this book didn't work out for me. I was so ready to love this but shit happened. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ <br><br><u>Okay. I'll start with what I liked about this book:</u><br><b>1.</b> The fact that Exy is a co-ed sport and that it doesn't matter how tall you are to play this game. And that teeny-tiny bit about second chances. <br><b>2.</b> I got this for free on Kindle.<br><b>3.</b> Umm... I think that's it? I almost added how it has openly gay characters but when I think of Nicky and how he annoyed me so much, <i>I just can't do it.</i> LGBTQ+ rep characters are good so please don't make me hate them.<br><br><b>Now on to the things that made me pull my hair out a.k.a. Why I Think This Book is Trash, shall we?</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524058510ra/25396810.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As a writer myself, I do pay a lot of attention to the writing style of the book I'm reading. That is personally what makes or breaks a book for me. I notice a lot of tiny details like how a particular paragraph flows or if the transition was good, etc. It doesn't really take much to impress me, I mean, I read smutty books that are 99.9% sex scenes and only 0.01% logical plot. I don't mind very simple writing as long as you can relay your story. (Think fairy tales!)<br><br>But man, THIS BOOK. (!!!) <br><br>My main problem with the book is the writing style. It was stunted and awkward and worsened my reading experience. I found myself rereading several passages over and over again just to see if I read <i>that totally absurd scene</i> correctly. It fucking tested my comprehension skill. I feel like the writing style is being purposefully difficult so that it can hide just how fucking terrible everything is in this book. As one reviewer said, <i>It's like the book is screaming at your face, "I'm trying really hard to be difficult to follow. Can you see the difficulty?" Well, book, you shall be pleased with yourself because not only did I see the difficulty, I felt it in my very bones.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524060299ra/25396900.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>SAME, GURL. SAME.<br><br>Every chapter is info-dumpy, too much irrelevant talk and legit nothing was happening. It was too descriptive in the wrong parts. Like I don't get enough descriptions on how the characters looked, their mannerisms, etc. (except for Andrew always hurting someone when they wake him up) I can't even tell how most of the characters looked like. It became so exhausting to read I even had a mini-slump halfway in the story. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Exy was a bastard sport, an evolved sort of lacrosse on a soccer-sized court with the violence of ice hockey, and Neil loved every part of it from its speed to its aggression."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Another thing I hated about this book: EXY. <br><br>As a sports fan, the fact that the author invented her own sport without clearly any idea of how <i>real</i> sports worked just irked me so much. Was it laziness? Because there are tons of sports out there and all you have to do is do something called research. Maybe it's because she wanted a co-ed sport but still, I just hate how messy this fantasy sport is. Given that it is a very significant part of the story, it wasn't given much thought. Sorry, but this is not acceptable to me. <br><br>You want to create something new? Well at least make it realistic. (QUIDDITCH, BITCH!) I find it so absurd that someone can just create a sport out of nothing and make it one of the most popular sports worldwide in only 30 years? Even Quidditch took hundreds of years to be popular! <br><br>Unrealistic things about Exy:<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"His decision to turn the Foxhole Court into a halfway house of sorts was nice in theory, but it meant his players were fractured isolationists who couldn't get along long enough to get through a game."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>- That is some fucking fantasy. <i>Please.</i> Team sports don't work like that. Even a football player with an inflated ego would know that you can't go anywhere with a team like that.<br>- Drugs. No way a coach would let his players get away with that. And hello, there's this little thing, that doesn't always work tbh, but sometimes does...called antidoping you know? <br>- Professional players training on their own, without their coach. AHHAAHAHA THIS IS A JOKE.<br>- a pro team without reserve players on their roster?<br>- A professional player refusing to train with his teammates, save for two of them. <i>Are. You. Fucking. Kidding. Me?</i> <br>- A player carrying knives on the court. WTF?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Wymack rarely interfered in the fighting. He let them brawl and then punished them with intense cardio and excruciating drills. Seemed he'd long ago decided his team could only function by testing themselves against each other and establishing their own ranking."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>- And a lame ass coach. If you have no authority over your players I suggest you go home, man. <br><br>AND IT'S OFFICIAL. THIS BOOK'S CHAPTER 11 IS THE LONGEST AND MOST USELESS CHAPTER I'VE EVER READ IN MY LIFE. It's basically a second after second telling of what happened in the most boring game in history. <br><br>Another thing that just frustrated me and had thrown me deep into the nine levels of hell is how little research the author made regarding everything mental health-related she used in this book. <i>God.</i> <b>The things that were written here only perpetuates stigma against mental illnesses and people who are affected by them.</b> The author made these stereotypical characters and made them behave in a disgusting way that is no way related to these illnesses. Words like suicide and psychotic were thrown around lightly in this book that just profoundly displeased me. I have a lot to say about this, but I suggest you check out my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/notes/18874651-the-foxhole-court/22594701-d-i-a-n-n-a?page=1&amp;ref=rsp" rel="nofollow noopener">notes and highlight in this book.</a> Just beware, there might be spoilers ahead, so I advise you not to check them out if you haven't read the book.<br><br>Also, if I got it correctly: A court-induced mania? Is that real? Because that sounds disturbing to me. Like who would want mania? Who thought it's a good idea to force someone to develop mania just to lessen aggressive behavior??? Wtf. Shouldn't it be more on the likes of anger management or something? Or is the author trying to use <a href="https://mentalillnesspolicy.org/kendras-law/kendras-law-overview.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Kendra's Law</a> here but can't put it into words correctly? Or <i>maybe</i> the use of the word mania here is incorrect? I definitely think so.<br><br>And as if I hadn't had enough of this torture, there's even some kind of rape joke! <i>Tadaaaaaaaaa!</i> <br><br><b>The one thing I was excited about this book is that people told me there's gay romance here. But honestly, I can't see myself enjoying a romance in which the MC falls for someone who forced himself on him, or drugged him, or kidnapped him, threatened him several times or bullied him. It's not okay just because they're boys and not girls. Unhealthy relationships shouldn't be justified because "boys will be boys."</b><br><br>Aaaaaand, if your family drugs you, makes you drink when you don't want to, take knives to family games, has a member who is a psychopath, threatens to kill you and even tries a couple times....... Yep, that sounds like family to me.<br><br>I almost forgot how fucking bland the characters are too. I felt like the author's recipe for these characters are annoying, boring, and everything not nice. <br><br>Like the ACOTAR series, I've heard that this series is so good, and that the first book isn't that great and that I'd have to push through it, but one can only push through so much. At this moment, I can't say that I'll read the following books in the series. If you enjoyed this book, good for you. Seriously, I'm happy for you. Maybe my bullshit shield is just so much more sensitive nowadays.<br><br><br><b>ya girl is just going to gather my receipts and then I'll get back to anyone with the full review</b><br>buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword" rel="nofollow noopener">the Percy</a> to my Monty</span>
  <a data-text-id="9155843782683179058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
