  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1614770349" />
    <a title="Lisa Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26649628-lisa-johnson"><img alt="Lisa Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589956286p2/26649628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1614770349?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Johnson" href="/user/show/26649628-lisa-johnson">Lisa Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26649628-lisa-johnson?shelf=involves-sports">involves-sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26649628-lisa-johnson?shelf=character-driven">character-driven</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1614770349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11429421874821506503"><b>Let me introduce you to my most recent obsession:</b><br/><br/><a href='http://de.tinypic.com?ref=30waszp' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463496381i/19125002.png' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Remember this feeling. This is the moment you stop being the rabbit.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Oh, joy. I have gracefully avoided writing a review on any of these books until I have read them all, because I honestly couldn't stop reading until I was through with the whole trilogy.<br/><br/>Now I don't remember my feelings on this first book anymore because I am overwhelmed by the <i>GREATNESS</i> that is contained in the other two books.<br/><br/>So now, my review will consist of:<br/><br/><b>
  <u>REASONS</u></b></span>
  <span id="freeText11429421874821506503" style="display:none"><b>Let me introduce you to my most recent obsession:</b><br><br><a href="http://de.tinypic.com?ref=30waszp" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463496381i/19125002.png" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“Remember this feeling. This is the moment you stop being the rabbit.”</i>
</b><br><br>Oh, joy. I have gracefully avoided writing a review on any of these books until I have read them all, because I honestly couldn't stop reading until I was through with the whole trilogy.<br><br>Now I don't remember my feelings on this first book anymore because I am overwhelmed by the <i>GREATNESS</i> that is contained in the other two books.<br><br>So now, my review will consist of:<br><br><b>
  <u>REASONS WHY YOU SHOULD READ THE ALL FOR THE GAME TRILOGY BY NORA SAKAVIC</u>
</b><br><br>● First of all, <b>the first book is free</b>, and the other two are under a pound each. Like, you <i>legally</i> get this whole trilogy in all its glory for under two pounds. Why wouldn't you give it a try? You have literally nothing to lose. You can also buy paperback versions of this on Amazon for about ten pounds each, but as I prefered the inexpensive version, I read all three books on my phone, the first one on my kindle app and the other two on iBooks. I do think I might purchase the physical copies now, though, because I WANT them on my shelf.<br>● <b>The characters.</b> All of these people are so complex and interesting and flawed. Seriously, especially if you are a fan of The Raven Cycle (which is pretty character-driven IMO), you might want to have a look into this.<br><b>
  <i>"How are you getting along with your teammates?" "I'm pretty sure the majority of them are clinically insane."</i>
</b><br>● <b>The sports.</b> Now, hear me out. I am literally the least sportive person in the world. I don't care about any sport in the slightest and the only time I ever do is the FIFA World Cup (feeling of companionship and unity, yada yada, you know.) I thought the sport aspect would bore me, but it absolutely didn't. If you've read and liked <i>Winger</i> by Andrew Smith, it's a bit like that, but so much more intriguing, because Nora invented this particular kind of sport for the series itself, and the history and background is just so cool. Trust me, you might end up loving it. If not, do not despair - there's so much more to it, Exy is only a part of a whole.<br>● <b>Issues.</b> Like, okay, I would have to give a lot of trigger warnings for this one, including mental and physical abuse, drug use, rape, mentions of self-harm, depression... Everything you can think of, basically. But this is exactly what I think contributes to making this story so deep and the characters so complex and what eventually also contributes to topics being addressed such as the importance of consent, the importance of family and friendship, the importance of having a purpose in life.<br>● <b>LGBT.</b> Not really a spoiler - there are gay and demisexual characters and it's very well-handled, in my opinion. Good writing.<br><b>
  <i>“I don't swing either way.”<br>“Bullshit,” Nicky said.<br>“I don't.”<br>[...]<br>“When you say you don't like being touched, is it because you don't like it at all or because you don't trust anyone else enough to let them touch you?”<br>“It doesn't matter.”<br>“If it didn't, I wouldn't ask.”<br>“It doesn't matter to a man who doesn't swing.”<br>[...]<br>“I've said all year I don't swing and I mean it. Kissing you doesn't make me look at any of them differently. The only one I'm interested in is you.”</i>
</b><br>● <b>The plot.</b> It might not <i>sound</i> very interesting when you first look at the synopsis, but it <i>is</i>, it so is.<br>● <b>Andrew Joseph Minyard.</b> Who is basically like Ronan Lynch and Joseph Kavinsky in one person. I love him.<br><b>
  <i>"Honesty suited Andrew because he was an instigator at heart and his opinions were often unpopular."<br>"Tick tock, says the clock. Get out of my room.“</i>
</b><br><br>So in conclusion: The writing is well done, the characters are complex and interesting and <i>real</i>, the plot is thrilling and disturbing and all-encompassing at times and makes you think a lot about some things, there is diversity and it's basically free.<br><br>Also, the series gets better with each book. The Foxhole Court was pretty good, The Raven King was oooooomg and The King's Men was just unbelievably awesome. This series has quickly become a favourite of mine and I think it should be more known and <i>out there</i>, because it's so so underrated.<br><br><b>
  <i>“This is about everything it took you to get to this point, everything it cost you, and everyone who laughed when you dared to dream of something big and bright. You're here tonight because you refused to give up and refused to give in. You're here where they all said you'd never be, and no one can say you haven't earned the right to play this game. All eyes are on you. It's time to show them what you're made of. There's no room for doubt, no room for second guesses, no room for error. This is your night. This is your game. This is your moment. Seize it with everything you've got. Pull out all the stops and lay it all on the line. Fight because you don't know how to die quietly. Win because you don't know how to lose. This king's ruled long enough—it's time to tear his castle down.” </i>
</b><br><br><br><b>READ IT. YOU'RE WELCOME.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11429421874821506503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656948823" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16078761360319727902"><i>“It’s not the world that’s cruel. It’s the people in it.”</i><br/><br/>Man, this book. I don't remember the last time a story captured me as much as this one did. I totally forgot about my surroundings, read till late at night and couldn't get enough. That's what makes for a great book.<br/><br/>The many characters and the fact that I've never read a sports book before confused me in the beginning. But especially the characters. They are mean, have hidden motives and complicated pasts.<br/>Andrew is the biggest bully on the</span>
  <span id="freeText16078761360319727902" style="display:none"><i>“It’s not the world that’s cruel. It’s the people in it.”</i><br /><br />Man, this book. I don't remember the last time a story captured me as much as this one did. I totally forgot about my surroundings, read till late at night and couldn't get enough. That's what makes for a great book.<br /><br />The many characters and the fact that I've never read a sports book before confused me in the beginning. But especially the characters. They are mean, have hidden motives and complicated pasts.<br />Andrew is the biggest bully on the lot. He makes me mad. He's ruthless and aggressive and doesn't respect boundaries. It doesn't hurt to not be an ass, and the way Andrew treats people is inexcusable.<br />Nicky is another two-faced bully. That's why I was glad for all the good people on the team. Matt and Dan, Renee and Coach. All of those character have incredible character-depth and seem so real. Their relationships and stories fascinated me. I just have to keep reading this series to know where everything is going.<br /><br />The plot was okay. It was a very character driven book, so there was enough excitement as it is. But I'm hoping for more suspense in the sequel. And more romance! What happened to the promised m/m romance? Or romance in general? Cause there was not a single trace anywhere. So I was waiting for the gay and not getting it. That, however, is not the authors fault, but the genres the book is sorted into.<br /><br />Anyway, I'm glad the sequels gave me the romance I was waiting for. This is such an amazing series.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_2766028838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2766028838" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2766028838?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781516801510" href="/book/show/29810275-the-foxhole-court">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=sports">sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2766028838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16198202067777730825"><b>Buddy Read, Part One</b> with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2602622093' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alison</a>! ;)<br/><br/><i>Actual rating</i>: <b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565376334ra/27963557.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>I'm sorry; I had to! xD</i> (In case you DID want to know...foxes bark like dogs!)<br/><br/>Calling this a <b>gay mafia sports romance</b> trilogy is a pretty accurate description! <br/><br/>It's about <b>Neil</b>, who is a player of this really weird sport called <b>Exy</b> (more on that later), who is recruited by the <b>worst-ranked team</b> in their division (<i>the Foxes</i>), which is comprised of a band of seriously messed up misfits (especially that nutter, Andrew)...while simultaneousl</span>
  <span id="freeText16198202067777730825" style="display:none"><b>Buddy Read, Part One</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2602622093" rel="nofollow noopener">Alison</a>! ;)<br><br><i>Actual rating</i>: <b>2.5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565376334ra/27963557.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I'm sorry; I had to! xD</i> (In case you DID want to know...foxes bark like dogs!)<br><br>Calling this a <b>gay mafia sports romance</b> trilogy is a pretty accurate description! <br><br>It's about <b>Neil</b>, who is a player of this really weird sport called <b>Exy</b> (more on that later), who is recruited by the <b>worst-ranked team</b> in their division (<i>the Foxes</i>), which is comprised of a band of seriously messed up misfits (especially that nutter, Andrew)...while simultaneously worrying about an extension of the yakuza, who funds the rival, <b>best-ranked team</b> (<i>the Ravens</i>). <br><br>Maybe I've read too much <b>NA sports romance</b> and <b>NA mafia romance</b>, but this book tried to tackle <i>TOO MUCH</i>. It's like the author went, "<i>Mafia romance? Sports romance? Hey! Why not BOTH?!</i>" This choice just made the plot of the book seem too <b>far-fetched</b>, making the novel come across more as <b>well-written fanfiction</b>, than a genuine book. I mean, it was just so...<i>RIDICULOUS</i>. Sakavic should have chosen one topic, rather than both. It would've made for a much stronger book.<br><br>I don't know what you consider to be spoilers or not, so read the remainder of my review at your own risk. Aka: <b>SPOILER ALERT!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565382737ra/27963852.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's start with the characters. I'll be honest. The only one I actually care about is <b>Neil</b>. That's it. He's my darling cinnamon roll. My poor, abused and scarred baby. Should any harm come to him...imma gonna shoot someone. <i>AND THAT'S A PROMISE</i>. I do love the trope of <b>found families</b> though, so hopefully my precious Neil will end this trilogy with the support system he <i>DESERVES</i>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565382021ra/27963825.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everyone else? Meh. *<i>shrugs</i>* My second-favourite was <b>Coach Wymack</b>. Although I liked him, for someone who professed wanting to give his players <b>another chance</b> at life, a do-over essentially (which he admittedly did -- I especially liked the scene where he told Neil that he'd never put his hands on him)...he was such <b>an enabler</b>! What kind of coach permits drugs and alcohol?! Do the players not get drug tested?! What kind of coach permits such violent behaviour?! The ones I've met have always wanted a united team and basically forced them to be one, but Wymack just let them go at each other's throats! What the heck?! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565382737ra/27963853.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Moving on to <b>Andrew</b>...oh boy, is this bloke <i>PSYCHOTIC</i>. He just goes around throwing people against walls, hitting them with Exy racquets, threatening them with knives, drugging them against their will, blackmailing them, basically controlling what friends Kevin is permitted to have...the list goes on! (Yes, I know his backstory already, but that doesn't justify it). I found <b>nothing good</b> about his character. <b>Kevin</b> went from being a <i>bully</i> one second to a <i>doormat</i> the next. <b>Nicky</b> was also sketchy (I guess it runs in the family lol). He did a lot of things that I was <i>uncomfortable</i> with. <b>Just give Neil his space!</b> I <i>ADORED</i> <b>Matt</b>! He definitely had that older brother personality. I loved how <b>protective</b> he was of Neil. <i>I &lt;3 him.</i> <b>Riko</b> was more like a caricature of a villain, rather than being an actual one. Everyone else was pretty <b>one dimensional</b> and <b>under-developed</b>, so I don't have much to say about them.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565380656ra/27963756.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, <b>Exy</b>. Oh dear. Why?! <i>WHY</i> make up a <b>fake sport</b> that is essentially just lacrosse? (The only fake sport that I'm interested in is <b>Quidditch</b>, thank you very much. <i>FLYING BROOMS</i>). It's not like people don't like sports books! I don't play a single sport currently, but I still enjoy reading books about <i>football, US football (rugby with padding), hockey, Formula One, boxing, kickboxing, swimming, skiing, etc</i>. <b>IT IS LACROSSE</b>. There is literally a <b>lacrosse racquet</b> on one of the book covers! If I'm being honest, I was just playing out various lacrosse games from <i>Teen Wolf</i> in my head whilst reading, haha. <br><br>This entire book felt like a rather slow, 200-page <b>prologue</b>. Not much occurred, except for the last <b>25 pages</b>. I think that this trilogy would have been better suited as a <i>duology</i>. As someone who can read 600-800 page books in one sitting --if I'm interested enough, it should not have taken me <b>three days</b> to get through <b>200 pages</b>. Regardless, I have heard that these <i>get better</i> as the trilogy goes on, so I'm excited for that, even though I already partially know what happens, being the <b>Spoiler Queen</b> that I am. ;)<br><br>So...I <i>LIKED</i> this, but I didn't <i>LOVE</i> it. *<i>shrugs</i>*</span>
  <a data-text-id="16198202067777730825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2726880792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2726880792" />
    <a title="tappkalina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32352828-tappkalina"><img alt="tappkalina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542817471p2/32352828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2726880792?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="tappkalina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="tappkalina" href="/user/show/32352828-tappkalina">tappkalina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781516801510" href="/book/show/29810275-the-foxhole-court">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=favourite-characters">favourite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=lgbt-read">lgbt-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=fave-shelf">fave-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=hit-close-to-home">hit-close-to-home</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2726880792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7865261511415363529"><b>Guys, the first book is free on Kindle! Go, go, go!</b><br/><br/> <br/>10 June 2020<br/> <br/><b>
  <blockquote>"Remember this feeling. This is the moment you stop being the rabbit."</blockquote>
</b><br/>This is the book that understands me the best. Neil is the person I can relate to the most. Of course we don't have the same background, but I still see myself in him.<br/>Especially the <i>"I don't believe in family."</i> part.<br/>I don’t believe blood makes family and I cry every time someone who doesn’t have anyone finds a family for themself. <br/>Everyone has that one book t</span>
  <span id="freeText7865261511415363529" style="display:none"><b>Guys, the first book is free on Kindle! Go, go, go!</b><br /><br /> <br />10 June 2020<br /> <br /><b>
  <blockquote>"Remember this feeling. This is the moment you stop being the rabbit."</blockquote>
</b><br />This is the book that understands me the best. Neil is the person I can relate to the most. Of course we don't have the same background, but I still see myself in him.<br />Especially the <i>"I don't believe in family."</i> part.<br />I don’t believe blood makes family and I cry every time someone who doesn’t have anyone finds a family for themself. <br />Everyone has that one book that's just gets them, and this book/series is the one for me.<br /><blockquote>"I'm —" Neil didn't want to say it, but the word was already there, broken and pathetic between them, "— nothing. I'll always have and be nothing."</blockquote><br />What this boy had to endure during his childhood is unspeakable, and although I can tell you this much -<br /><blockquote>Neil stepped over it and went to stand in front of Wymack: within arm's reach but just barely. He'd perfected that trick as a kid. He could look at anyone's arms and judge the safe distance from them in a heartbeat. If they had to move to hit him, he had enough time to dodge. Either way he wouldn't catch the full intended force of their blow.</blockquote><br />- we doesn’t understand the full force of it until book 3.<br /><i>
  <blockquote>He wondered if he was supposed to feel something besides shock, but a mental check came back clean. He'd grown up around death. It was nothing to him now but ice in his system and a reminder to keep moving.</blockquote>
</i><br />The way Neil and Andrew slowly learn to trust each other is the most beautiful thing ever, even if both of them want something from the other at the beginning.<br /><b>
  <blockquote>Andrew didn't budge beneath his weight. He was something solid to lean against, something violent and fierce and unmoving. Neil couldn't remember what it felt like to have someone hold him up. It was terrifying and liberating all at once. His life was out of his control now; he was giving it to Andrew and hoping Andrew would keep it safe.</blockquote>
</b><br /><blockquote>[…] trying to remember the last time someone gave him a gift and coming up blank. That his first one should be from Andrew was unsettling.</blockquote><br />I loved the others the first time I read the book, but now I learned to truly appretiate them. Matt and Dan are the best parent figures Neil could ever have and they are doing their best to protect him.<br /><blockquote>"I'm fine," Neil said. [...]<br />"You say that an awful lot," Matt said. "I'm starting to think you don't know what it means."</blockquote><br />Waymack, our dearest godfather sends y’all his message:<br /><b>
  <blockquote>"It's about second chances, Neil. Second, third, fourth, whatever, as long as you get at least one more than what anyone else wanted to give you."</blockquote>
</b><br />The last page, especially the last sentence brings tears to my eyes every. fucking. time. <br /><blockquote>Neil looked down at the key in his hand. "Home," he whispered, needing to hear it aloud. It was a foreign concept to him, an impossible dream. It was frightening and wonderful all at once, and it set his heart racing so fast he thought it'd drum out of his chest. "Welcome home, Neil."</blockquote><br /><br /> <br />20 September 2019 <br /><br />Two words: Neil. Josten. ♡</span>
  <a data-text-id="7865261511415363529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1963543476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963543476" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963543476?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=ya-na-contemporaries">ya-na-contemporaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1963543476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10993192341030684758">Thinking about it twice, and at the risk of getting <s>lynched</s> hardcore side-eyed forever, I must admit that I didn't like this as much as I thought I would. <br/>I don't know, we just didn't...click. <br/>The writing was a bit <i>meh</i> and the characters...well, they weren't awful (or were they?) but let's say I'm not exactly a fan.<br/>All my friends seem to like/adore/worship this series, and then there's me. Not giving an absolute darn. <br/>Takes all sorts, I guess.<br/>What can I say, c'est la vie. <br/>¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png' width='80' height='80' alt='Professional Reader' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png' width='80' height='80' alt='10 Book Reviews' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png' width='80' height='80' alt='Reviews Published' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></span>
  <span id="freeText10993192341030684758" style="display:none">Thinking about it twice, and at the risk of getting <s>lynched</s> hardcore side-eyed forever, I must admit that I didn't like this as much as I thought I would. <br>I don't know, we just didn't...click. <br>The writing was a bit <i>meh</i> and the characters...well, they weren't awful (or were they?) but let's say I'm not exactly a fan.<br>All my friends seem to like/adore/worship this series, and then there's me. Not giving an absolute darn. <br>Takes all sorts, I guess.<br>What can I say, c'est la vie. <br>¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Professional Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png" width="80" height="80" alt="10 Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Reviews Published" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1733124097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1733124097" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1733124097?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18874651-the-foxhole-court">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1733124097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4830045143131606094"><b>
  <u>This novel is about Neil Josten.</u>
</b><br/><br/>✘ Freshmen at Palmetto State University.<br/>✘ Hiding from his ruthless, crime boss father. <br/>✘ Obsessed with Exy.<br/>✘ Runs faster than you.<br/><br/>Generally when someone says <i>"This book reads like fanfiction,"</i> that is not a compliment. It usually means one or more of the following things: <br/><br/>- The characters are unbelievable.<br/>- The main character is a self-insert and/or they are the epitome of perfection.<br/>- Typos. Grammatical Errors. Misspellings.<br/>- The plot is nonexistent or poorly</span>
  <span id="freeText4830045143131606094" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>This novel is about Neil Josten.</u>
</b><br /><br />✘ Freshmen at Palmetto State University.<br />✘ Hiding from his ruthless, crime boss father. <br />✘ Obsessed with Exy.<br />✘ Runs faster than you.<br /><br />Generally when someone says <i>"This book reads like fanfiction,"</i> that is not a compliment. It usually means one or more of the following things: <br /><br />- The characters are unbelievable.<br />- The main character is a self-insert and/or they are the epitome of perfection.<br />- Typos. Grammatical Errors. Misspellings.<br />- The plot is nonexistent or poorly constructed.<br />- 50 Shades of Grey *cue scary music*<br /><br /><b>In this case, I don't mean to imply <u>any of thee above.</u></b><br /><br />When I say this book reads like fanfiction, I mean I read it the same way I used to read some of my all-time favorite fanfiction stories back in the day. <b>With a joyful but ravenous intent.</b> <br /><br />It gave me that feeling I've had before where you're left staring at your computer screen wondering if maybe this anonymous author has portrayed truer versions of your favorites than their actual creators.<br /><br />The main characters here are literally a pack of <b>misfits &amp; troubled individuals,</b> and they're all absolute <i>savages,</i> which is perfectly fitting for such a wicked plot as this one. <br /><br />I said <i>"Oh my God"</i> and <i>"Jesus Christ"</i> out loud more times than I care to count while reading this, it was just <b>that entertaining.</b><br /><br />Also I took a particular liking to the sport Sakavic created for her team, Exy, which plays like a mash-up between Soccer &amp; Rugby with all the violence of Hockey. <br /><br />It's interesting to try and imagine how the game plays out on a court &amp; its brutality feels like a solid parallel to Neil's life, both on &amp; off his team.<br /><br />I also happen to find Neil's passion for it <b>quite charming.</b><br /><br />My only quip with this novel is the writing. <u>It's not that good, folks.</u><br /><br />It's not <i>dreadful,</i> but it lacks that polished <b>consistency</b> that comes from a professional editor. <br /><br />Names were repeated too often in some sections, not enough in others. A couple confusing leaps between events here &amp; there. Some cheesy dialogue that I can't imagine anyone saying in real life. <br /><br /><b>However, I'm definitely excited to find out more, as this installment is pretty short on answers about the overarching mystery that is Neil Josten. All in all, a strong, attention-getting debut.</b><br /><br /><i>Side note: Half-way through this I realized that if you squint the cover of this looks like 4 corn dogs about to be dipped in some corn dog-colored sauce...</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4830045143131606094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It is simply a joke, a not even well-written piece of a book that doesn't just lack of an actual plot but has the most boring, mind-blowingly annoying as f*ck characters I've met in a while. I congratulate myself for reading the entire thing. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406423131ra/10547319.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Neil Josten is the newest addition to the Palmetto State University Exy team. He's short, he's fast, he's got a ton of potential—and he's the runaway son of the murderous crime lord known a</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14541057603989466503" style="display:none">How did this book managed to get so much popularity on tumblr??? It is simply a joke, a not even well-written piece of a book that doesn't just lack of an actual plot but has the most boring, mind-blowingly annoying as f*ck characters I've met in a while. I congratulate myself for reading the entire thing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406423131ra/10547319.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Neil Josten is the newest addition to the Palmetto State University Exy team. He's short, he's fast, he's got a ton of potential—and he's the runaway son of the murderous crime lord known as The Butcher.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Knowing that he has to keep a low profile for the rest of his life if, you know, he wants to <i>stay alive</i>, Neil joins the Foxes. Who cares, <b>YOLO#</b> right?? The kid's been doing so well running away from the Japanese mafia and his father's enemies to start acting dumb now. Disappointed but not surprised. <br><br>OK, how can someone create an sport out of nothing and make it one of the most popular in only 30 (!!!) years??? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473962868i/20537087._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Too good to be true. Exy is a sort of mix between cricket and tennis? All I know is they use rackets and have a goalkeeper. I hardly remember the vague descriptions and that's because they made me even more confused. It was not clear to me how Exy worked and that's a shame because I love sports. <br><br>The Foxes are the <b>worst-ranked team of the league</b> yet they have a professional and ex champion playing for them. Anyone who understands how sports work would know that there's something fishy about Kevin being part the team. <b>They suck</b>. They literally have no replacement for their players. At all. Their coach allows them to use <b>DRUGS</b>, practice on their own or not even practice at all. <i>I am sorry but there's something called antidoping @ Nora Sak*vic.</i> <br><br>They barely had one match in the whole book, and they lost. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396955261ra/9209538.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The foxhole court was the only home he needed; the foxes were his family.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>If your family drugs you, makes you drink when you don't want to, takes knives to family games, has a member who is a psychopath, threatens to kill you and even tries a couple times....... Yep, that sounds like family to me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They're actually Lannisters <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Neil is boring. Kevin is pointless. Andrew is a drug-addict/psychopath/should be in jail/banned from ever playing Exy again moody teenager who will probably kill one of his team members in the future. Nicky is like that black friend who's always saying dumb and funny things in Hollywood comedies. Coach is the babysitter that has to handle their BS because the Foxes can never act like normal college athletes, God forbid them!!<br><br>Do not even try it. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5807973666688008545"><b>❥ 3 / 5 stars</b><br/><br/>oh god i have no idea where i should begin. there are lots of mixed feelings about it and it’s really hard to review. so, please don’t mind me if this review got a bit messy.<br/><br/>first of all, i think it must be my mistake that i have so little knowledge of sports which is the reason why i couldn’t get into this book as much as i should. so this one i blame myself then not the book. but the thing that i want more from the author is the explanation about <b>‘exy’</b> thing. i read until the end </span>
  <span id="freeText5807973666688008545" style="display:none"><b>❥ 3 / 5 stars</b><br /><br />oh god i have no idea where i should begin. there are lots of mixed feelings about it and it’s really hard to review. so, please don’t mind me if this review got a bit messy.<br /><br />first of all, i think it must be my mistake that i have so little knowledge of sports which is the reason why i couldn’t get into this book as much as i should. so this one i blame myself then not the book. but the thing that i want more from the author is the explanation about <b>‘exy’</b> thing. i read until the end and question marks are still popping in my head. it would be better if i could understand it more.<br /><br />second, since there are many unexpected things and situations occurring in the book so it might sound interesting because you couldn’t predict what will happen next in the story, right? i thought like that at first but when i read though it, ummm what should i say, it makes me got a question that <b>‘does this book really have a plot like this or the author just keep adding more and more stuff in the story?’</b> i hope it’s the former.<br /><br />third, talking about the situations, i don’t know if it’s only me or not but i think most of them are so unrealistic. i can’t deny that i enjoy reading it because i do. it’s really entertaining but yeah, it’s kinda unrealistic and it makes me feel uncomfortable.<br /><br />fourth, the author’s writing style. i think she could write it better than she did, i don’t know. maybe she write it well already but the problem is me myself or in fact, she didn’t write it well enough.<br /><br />fifth, the characters. i haven’t found my favorite character yet since many of them are err......... but it would be fun to know them better in the other books! i bet they also have a good side not only a bad one.<br /><br /><br />however, though i didn’t like it as much as i hoped, i’ll continue reading this trilogy because i extremely want to know what will happen in the story.<br /><br /><br /><b>p.s. the last 10% is the best part of the book and i loveeeeee it! </b></span>

<div id="review_1782749070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782749070" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56662187-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539790744p2/56662187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1782749070?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/56662187-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782749070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11997534121131800197">I initially read the Foxhole Court because people always compare it to the Raven Cycle which I love. And those people were right, but pretty early in the book I started to love it for what it is not just because it's similar to trc. These characters are complex and messy and so is their world. No, this isn't a book with magic, but it has crime lords, murderous fathers, and lovable teenage psychos. We follow one sports team's arc from people who are a danger to each other to people who protect ea</span>
  <span id="freeText11997534121131800197" style="display:none">I initially read the Foxhole Court because people always compare it to the Raven Cycle which I love. And those people were right, but pretty early in the book I started to love it for what it is not just because it's similar to trc. These characters are complex and messy and so is their world. No, this isn't a book with magic, but it has crime lords, murderous fathers, and lovable teenage psychos. We follow one sports team's arc from people who are a danger to each other to people who protect each other from danger. If you started to turn away with the words sports team, WAIT! Trust me I'm not a sports person either, but it's less about Exy, and more about the kids who play. <br /><br />This book is dark. These kids are messed up, and I loved it. The author doesn't resort to angst or frustrating miscommunications to move the plot along, and yet this book is full of messy relationships and people and situations. When you start you don't really understand anything that's going on, but that's what makes it so interesting. Slowly, we start to understand Neil and the other foxes and why they do the seemingly insane things that they do. It feels like a murder mystery book, but really it's about teenagers hitting each other on and off the court. They speak multiple languages, they do drugs, they get into fights. Is it the most realistic, real to life book ever? nooooo, but that's part of the appeal.<br /><br />Favorite character? Andrew Minyard. I do not understand him at all, but I will. I'm determined to. He's like Ronan Lynch and Kavinksy from trc combined into one highly medicated, angry, talented, and loyal individual. Why does he protect his people? Why is he able to? I couldn't tell you at this point, but I think he's the most complicated character I've read in a while. And obviously the character that the other characters in the book call a psycho is almost always my favorite.<br /><br />I was sucked into this book from start to finish. It helps that it is free on ibooks, but I'll probably end up buying a physical copy because I loved it so much. I could not stop reading it, and I've already got the next one downloaded and ready to go. (written at first read)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11997534121131800197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036026529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3545966952005992023"><i>"Welcome home, Neil."</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522429658ra/25298108.gif' width='250' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'll start by saying I absolutely fell in love with this book and this series and finished all of them in 3 days. This series is about a fictional sport, relationships, and INTRIGUE. Honestly I'm horrible at plot descriptions but I think this book works better if you go into it knowing as little as possible. Because non-sports fans will still probably love this even though that's a component of it.<br/><br/>The most special thing about this book for me was the complicated characteriza</span>
  <span id="freeText3545966952005992023" style="display:none"><i>"Welcome home, Neil."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522429658ra/25298108.gif" width="250" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll start by saying I absolutely fell in love with this book and this series and finished all of them in 3 days. This series is about a fictional sport, relationships, and INTRIGUE. Honestly I'm horrible at plot descriptions but I think this book works better if you go into it knowing as little as possible. Because non-sports fans will still probably love this even though that's a component of it.<br><br>The most special thing about this book for me was the complicated characterization. If you've read any of my reviews you know that <b>characterization is the #1 thing that can make or break a book for me (world building can choke idc).</b> And this book truly stands apart from anything else I've read. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523029092ra/25335168.gif" width="200" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>None of the characters introduced are flat and that SHOCKED me since there was so damn many of them (blame the sports aspect I guess). I also appreciated that characters with trauma actually exhibited those signs and didn't automatically become chipper and cured when someone was nice to them? <br><br>There was nothing about this book that I didn't love. However, I will say that the writing style might bother others. The language is NOT at all flowery, and I've heard some describe it as "telling not showing." I personally think that the writing worked really well given the subject matter and the main character and it didn't distract from the story itself. But that being said having read reviews before reading this I was able to see how some could be bothered.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1621350241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14149147980163931485">Reread 2018: Listen it’s 11:57 and I have 3 pages left. I finished it before midnight even if I had half a page left. <br/><br/>I just needed to be back here with these characters. <br/><br/><br/>————————————————————<br/><br/><br/><br/>Reread 2017: I forgot how slow this first book is. I love it, and it's essential for the whole trilogy, but on its own it does not offer much. I will say though this book holds its own in the trilogy because without a strong start this series would fall apart. <br/><br/>------------------------------------------------</span>
  <span id="freeText14149147980163931485" style="display:none">Reread 2018: Listen it’s 11:57 and I have 3 pages left. I finished it before midnight even if I had half a page left. <br /><br />I just needed to be back here with these characters. <br /><br /><br />————————————————————<br /><br /><br /><br />Reread 2017: I forgot how slow this first book is. I love it, and it's essential for the whole trilogy, but on its own it does not offer much. I will say though this book holds its own in the trilogy because without a strong start this series would fall apart. <br /><br />------------------------------------------------<br /><br />The thing you need to understand before I write this review is that when it comes to making me read a book, I'm easy. You literally just have to say "this is good" or "I liked this" and I'll probably be interested. It's why I'm an obsessive book buyer, I buy anything I've heard of. <br />So backtrack to February. My friend Miranda tells me that there's a series all over tumblr that everyone is obsessed with. She says it's amazing. So naturally I'm sold. But I don't read Ebooks so I wait 2 months for them to get published and another month for it to get to me. <br />And what did I know about these books? Zilch. I couldn't have told you a single thing about them. I assumed lacrosse based on the cover of book 3, but otherwise nothing. <br />What I ended up finding was fantastic. <br /><br />This is an extremely amazing character driven world. I LOVED the characters. And by love I mean I love how Sakavic wrote them. I actually despised 99% of them, but she wrote them so well, so realistic, that it's so good. This isn't a plot driven story. Yes there's a plot and it's intriguing and fast paced, but it's also not about the plot. It's about the characters and their relationships. <br /><br /><br />Which brings me to the best part of the book. THERES NO ROMANCE!!!! None. Not even a little bit of an inkling. There are 2 minor relationships that aren't even mentioned basically. It's fantastic. The drama in this book is "real!" And the quotations are because like this is not a realistic story. But still. <br />It's kind of funny to me that 85 people on Goodreads have shelved this book m/m romance since there's none at all. <br /><br />I wanted to rate this 4.5 stars but I bumped it to 5 stars because of the shocking ending. The way Sakavic delivered it had me gasping. The character's mannerisms made it such a well done and shocking moment. <br /><br />Definite must read series. <br /><br />And if you're still not sold: book 1 is free on Amazon/kindle etc and book 2 and 3 are 1$. This entire series can cost you only 2$ if you get the Ebooks. So worth it. <br /><br /><br /><i>Around The Year in 52 Books Challenge #52 - A book published in 2016 (Since I bought the physical copies I'm using their publishing date)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14149147980163931485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_704226247" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/704226247" />
    <a title="Ais" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8581195-ais"><img alt="Ais" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373253857p2/8581195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/704226247?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ais" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ais" href="/user/show/8581195-ais">Ais</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=really-good">really-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=recd-by-friend">recd-by-friend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=slash">slash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8581195-ais?shelf=death-and-other-assorted-sundries">death-and-other-assorted-sundries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704226247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12518641935952567791">Okay. Let me just say. This book is awesome. I pretty much fell in love with it from the beginning and I was happy to see that my affection for it didn't waver at all throughout.<br/><br/>Anyone who knows me probably knows I really love dark and twisted things. I really love to get to know what makes a character tick, and why do they react as they do, and along those lines I love seeing said reactions and getting the reason for it later rather than being told from the start what everything means. I love f</span>
  <span id="freeText12518641935952567791" style="display:none">Okay. Let me just say. This book is awesome. I pretty much fell in love with it from the beginning and I was happy to see that my affection for it didn't waver at all throughout.<br /><br />Anyone who knows me probably knows I really love dark and twisted things. I really love to get to know what makes a character tick, and why do they react as they do, and along those lines I love seeing said reactions and getting the reason for it later rather than being told from the start what everything means. I love figuring things out along the way. I love lots of things, but mostly I love things that don't bore or frustrate me.<br /><br />I went into this expecting I wouldn't be that into it because truefax, I don't like sports. I figured whether it was a made up sport or not would not affect my ability to focus on a book about something I don't like. Boy, was I wrong. Although Exy is a lot of the reasons for why people meet and interact, and there are scenes involving Exy games, the story is not about Exy. It's about all these characters who are varying levels of fucked up, and it's about figuring out why a little bit but mostly they're so awesome together I would have been content even without knowing why. And that's a feat because my sense of curiosity is as intense as a dead cat's.<br /><br />One of the things I think is coolest about this book/series is that she doesn't rely on the usual handicaps for moving things along. Silly misunderstandings aren't the main source of drama in this because even without misunderstandings there's plenty going on that keeps everyone in varying levels of truth and lie and obscurity. The things that happen all make sense. They don't feel contrived. They may feel like, "Whoa holy shit, what's up with that?" and "Why did s/he ___?" but it's because we don't yet know the reason for it, and when we do get the reason, even then it's bit by bit.<br /><br />I'm not doing a good job of explaining why this delighted me so much, but it did. It was more like a true mystery without the overtures of going into it blustering about making it a True Mystery. Sometimes I can feel the weight of an author pressing on the plot or characters to make this or that happen, but I didn't feel like that at all in this. I felt like things were unraveling as they went, and we got just enough information at a time to understand the basic context of why Neil thought this or did that, but even then we never got the whole story at once. Like Neil is so guarded he keeps secrets from, and lies to, even the reader.<br /><br />Freaking awesome, I tell you.<br /><br />I don't want to give spoilers so I won't go into specifics on anything, but if you couldn't tell, I heart this book. And I heart this author for writing it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12518641935952567791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oT/wams6SYPAO2EkR8iDuy02ujh0kLOG3SlHH3YHxBqfEXEe/S9XbE0maYZiN9zERkQQgtQZoZPK17QE8FNOIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fvFSEkyi38pNY2ULQSgWgueSaTp3qHNj/0uZWrReubxA39Nm2rfBJcB+balk10n9jODDgNchYXbotWpBMgozhA==')})
  }
